Jiexī Sàn: This formula treats infants with common colds or fevers, characterized by a red, flushed face, fever throughout the body, stiffness in the neck and similar symptoms. When combined with Rénshēn Sàn, the fever may subside later on. The severity of the condition can be observed; if the symptoms are mild, with a pulse that is not rapid or strong, a face that is not overly red, and no increased irritability—just some groaning and murmuring—this indicates a lighter condition, but only this formula should be administered.

Ingredients:

  • Ginseng, vine of Diao (钓藤), Platycodon, licorice, and Chuanxiong, each 3 qian (approximately 9 grams).
  • A 1 qian (around 3 grams) of stir-fried Qingli (葶苈).
  • 2 qian (about 6 grams) of white Poria.
  • 49 pieces of apricot kernel.
  • 4 liang (approximately 150 grams) of gypsum, calcined, and Ephedra (麻黄), with stems removed.

This combination should be ground into a fine powder. Each dose should be 2 qian, with one jujube and a cup of water, boiled down to half a cup to be taken. If the infant suffers from initial febrile illness, this medication should be administered first, ensuring careful recognition of symptoms. If it is measles, this medication should not be used. In cases of measles, the face appears pale and bluish, earlobes, knees, and tailbone feel cold like ice, the body is warm and strong, and signs of excitement and murmuring occur in dreams—these indicate that particular condition.

If a child with fever receives this Jiexī Sàn and gradually recovers, they can subsequently take Dà Guīmìng Sàn, Bǎoshòu Sàn, or Qingfěn Bái Zhú Sàn for further recuperation.[49p]
Baiyu Pill: This treats obstruction of phlegm and saliva in the diaphragm, alleviates persistent chest discomfort, and reduces coughing with excessive phlegm. Ingredients: Nanshing, Banxia, Jiangcan, and Baifan (both raw and cooked), each two and a half qian. Grind into a powder, add seven peeled apricot kernels and one Zao bean, mix well, and then form into pills the size of millet using the juice of peeled fresh ginger. Take 10 to 20 pills each time, swallowed with ginger soup, without time restrictions.

Pediatric Cough and Wheezing Method:

Six Gentlemen Decoction: This is for treating qi deficiency of the spleen and stomach that fails to nourish, leading to lung issues. Ingredients: Ginseng, Baizhu, Fuling, Licorice, Chenpi, and Banxia, each in equal quantities. For use, take two qian, decoct in ginger and jujube water.

Daqing Ointment: This treats lung excess combined with wind-cold, causing chest fullness, shortness of breath, and rapid, wheezing cough. Ingredients: Tianma and Qingtai, each one qian; Bai Fu (baked white attached), black snake meat soaked in wine and baked, and scorpion tail, both five fen; Tianzhuhuang and Musk, each one character. Grind into a powder, form into honey pills the size of beans, and take half a pill dissolved in mint soup.

Huangqin Lung Clearing Powder: This is for treating lung heat accompanied by difficulty in urination. Ingredients: One qian of Huangqin and one broken Ziziphus fruit.[50p]
The above text describes various traditional Chinese herbal formulas for specific ailments, along with their preparations and dosages.

  1. For Pain Relief:

    • Boil the ingredients in water for consumption. If ineffective, add 20 grains of salt and fermented soybeans.

  2. Daoshi Powder (for treating heat in the lung channel in children):

    • Ingredients: equal parts Rehmannia Root, Akebia, and Licorice.
    • Grind to a fine powder. Take one qian (approximately 3 grams) each time, add light bamboo leaves, boil in water.

  3. Yihuang Powder (for treating lung channel deficiency with symptoms including wheezing, facial flushing, heat, and phlegm):

    • Ingredients: 1 liang (approximately 30 grams) dried orange peel, 5 qian each of green peel, haritaki pulp, and roasted licorice, and 2 qian of clove.
    • Grind to a fine powder. Take two qian each time, boil in water.

  4. Qianghuo Powder (for tackling liver obstruction affecting the lungs with symptoms like wind sensitivity, dizziness, and confusion):

    • Ingredients: 0.5 liang each of Siler, Ligusticum, Ginseng, White Atractylodes, and red Poria; 1 liang of Gastrodia; and various other ingredients including dried silkworms and white flower snake meat, all in specific measurements.
    • Grind finely, combine with honey to form pills the size of broad beans. Take three pills before meals, either with mint soup or Ophiopogon soup. Caution: Do not take if there is real heat or severe fright, as it is warming in nature.[51p]
      Ginseng and Atractylodes Powder
      Treats spleen and lung deficiency with phlegm, symptoms include heaviness, vomiting phlegm, diarrhea, and cough.
      Ingredients: Ginseng, Atractylodes (stir-fried), Agastache leaves, Costus root, Licorice, White Poria (each one qian), Dried Kudzu (two qian).
      Method: Grind finely, add one slice of fresh ginger, one cup of water, boil down to seven parts, strain and take warm, without time restriction.

To treat cough, body heat with sticky phlegm, inability to digest milk and food, abdominal distension, and rough breathing.

Bai Xiang Pill: Treats children's cough with greenish vomiting.

Use red sprout cocklebur in appropriate amounts, dry it in the shade, boil with water until soft, remove the bones, expose it to sunlight until dry, then boil again with juice. Once the juice is completely evaporated, grind it into powder. Make small pills the size of millet, taking 10 to 20 pills each time and wash down with sesame soup, used as needed.

Crush all ingredients into powder, soak the black plums in wine overnight, remove the pits, steam, and mix with mashed rice to make pills the size of tung seeds. Take ten pills with warm water.

Elevated Hemp Decoction: Treats cough from the spleen, with pain under the right rib that radiates to the shoulder and back; severe cases may not allow movement, and moving causes coughing of phlegm. Ingredients: equal parts of licorice, white peony, elevated hemp, and dried kudzu. Crush into powder, take one penny each time, decoction with water.

Red Stone Fat and Remaining Grain Decoction: Treats cough from the large intestine with fecal incontinence. Ingredients: two taels each of red stone fat and remaining grain, crushed together. Take two pennies each time, decoction with water.

Ephedra and Aconite with Asarum Decoction: Treats cough from the kidneys, with pain in the lower back that radiates when soft, severe cases lead to coughing of phlegm. Also treats cold evils attacking the teeth, leading to pain in the brain teeth; should be used urgently, as delays may lead to lack of salvation. Ingredients: two pennies each of ephedra and asarum; one penny of aconite.[57p]
Right, take one qian each time, decoct in water.

Poria and Licorice Decoction treats bladder cough with urinary incontinence in cough. Poria two qian, cinnamon twig two and a half qian, five large slices of fresh ginger. Take two qian each time, decoct in water.

Xie Qing Pills treat facial redness from drinking, body heat with excessive phlegm, thick and sticky mucus, sore throat, wheezing, facial swelling, and vomiting food. Angelica, Sichuan lovage, and gentian root each one qian, rhubarb five fen, notopterygium, and gardenia fruit in equal parts. Grind into powder, form into honey pills the size of fox nuts. Take one pill, wash down with syrup. One formula adds licorice and peony.

Atractylodes Powder treats children’s cough with loss of internal fluids. One liang of atractylodes, lightly roasted, with each half liang of angelica, knotweed, lightly roasted, wood fragrance, and red peony, and honeyed licorice. Grind the medicine, sift roughly into powder. Take one qian each time, decoct in one small cup of water until reduced to five fen, strain, and adjust dosage according to child’s size without worrying about timing.

Wu Yao Decoction treats children’s red face and red lips, coarse breathing with fever, and cough with phlegm sounds. Use ma huang without removing the root nodes, apricot kernels without removing the skin tip, schizonepeta without removing the stems, and honey-water cooked and stir-fried platycodon, each five qian, with two and a half qian of licorice. Take two qian each time, with one cup of water, decoct until reduced to seven fen, and take warm without regard to time.[58p]
Qianghuo Powder treats the same condition as above.
Ingredients: Ginseng (remove the skin), Qianghuo, Red Poria (remove the skin), Chaihu (remove the skin), Xuanfu (remove the skin), Chuanxiong, Duhuo, Jiegang (cut and roast), Zhike, Cangzhu (process as previously), Licorice, each one tael. Grind together, take two qian per dose, with one cup of water, two slices of ginger, three leaves of mint, and boil down to seven parts. Take warm at any time. For dispersing wind pathogens, add green onion whites and simmer together.

Qingmuxiang Decoction treats the same condition as above.
Ingredients: Qingmuxiang, Zhike (soaked, remove the chaff and roast), each half a tael; Licorice two and a half qian. Use this blend, take two qian per dose, with one cup of water, boil down to seven parts, and take warm at any time.

Fuling Houpo Decoction treats children with pale lips and faces, cough, excessive sweating on the forehead, long exhalations, reduced milk intake, and vomiting.
Ingredients: White Poria and Banxia (boil and roast), each seven and a half qian; roasted Licorice three qian; Houpo five qian (remove the coarse skin and crush). For each kilogram of this mix, use one pound of fresh ginger cut into thin slices, pound and mix well, soak overnight, and dry by slow fire. Use this mixture, take two qian per dose, with one and a half cups of water, three slices of ginger, and boil down to seven parts. Take warm at any time. Optionally, add one jujube (remove the core) and simmer together.[59p]
Huo Xiang Decoction - Treats the same condition.
Ren Shen (Ginseng) and Ban Xia (Pinellia) as before, Chi Fu Ling (Red Poria) and Zhi Gan Cao (Honey-fried Licorice) each one tael, Cang Zhu (Atractylodes) soaked in rice water overnight and filtered, then sliced and stir-fried until slightly yellow, two taels; Chen Pi (Dried Tangerine Peel) and Huo Xiang each seven qian and five fen; Hou Po (Magnolia Bark) prepared, one tael and five fen.

Take this mixture, chew; each dose two qian, with one bowl of water, two slices of ginger, and one date, decoct until seven parts remain, taken warm on an empty stomach. Alternatively, add roasted salt and decoct together.

Li Zhong Decoction - Treats the same condition.
Ren Shen (Ginseng) and Bai Zhu (Atractylodes) each one tael, Gan Jiang (Dried Ginger) and Zhi Gan Cao (Honey-fried Licorice) each two qian and five fen.

Grind the above into a powder; each dose half qian or one qian, with warm plain water, taken on an empty stomach. Alternatively, add Xing Ren (Apricot Kernel) and Bei Wu Wei Zi (Schizandra) to decoct together.

Xing Pi San - Treats cough due to Spleen deficiency.
Bai Zhu (Atractylodes) roasted with wall earth, Ren Shen (Ginseng), Gan Cao (Licorice), Ji Hong (Tangerine Peel), Bai Fu Ling (White Poria), and Quan Xie (Scorpion) each half tael; Ban Xia (Pinellia) and Mu Xiang (Aucklandia) each one fen; Bai Fu (White Aconite) four pieces; Nan Xing (Nasty Star) two pieces, the above two ingredients each processed; Chen Cang rice two hundred grains.

Grind the above into a powder; each dose one qian, with half a bowl of water, two slices of ginger, and half a date, decoct until two parts remain, taken gradually. In another method, without Bai Zhu and Ban Xia, adding one qian of lotus meat is also acceptable.[60p]
Baifuzi Decoction treats severe wind-phlegm obstruction in children, where the wood element (liver) overcomes the earth element (spleen), leading to excessive coughing followed by vomiting, expelling both milk and phlegm, providing some relief.

Ingredients:

  • Baifuzi
  • Sheng Nanzhu
  • Sheng Banxia
  • Sheng Chuanwu (peeled and cored)
  • Ming Tianma
  • Chenpi
  • Nanmuxiang
  • Quanxie (tail and poisonous tip removed)
  • Jiangcan (silkworm, silk removed)
  • Dingxiang, each two qian.

Prepare by grinding the above, take two qian per dose, with one and a half cups of water, three slices of ginger, simmer over low heat for seven minutes, and take warm on an empty stomach five times.

Sanyao Decoction treats common cold with wind evil, nasal congestion with a heavy voice, inability to speak, or cold from wind causing headache and dizziness, stiffness in limbs, excessive coughing with phlegm, fullness in the chest, and shortness of breath.

Ingredients:

  • Mahuang (without joints)
  • Xingren (almonds without skins and tips)
  • Gancao (fresh)

Prepare by grinding the above in equal parts, take three qian per dose, with one cup of water and three slices of fresh ginger, simmer until reduced to six portions, strain and take warm, aiming to induce sweating.

An alternative includes adding Jingjie and Jiegeng. If cough is severe, add Wuweizi and Xixin, each reduced by half. Another formula substitutes Mahuang (without joints), Xingren (without skins and tips), and fried Gancao, named Sanhe Decoction, particularly effective for cough. Adjustments depend on individual treatments: add before Hu for heat, Jingjie for wind, and Banxia for phlegm.[61p]
Jia Jian San Yao Decoction
Ma Huang without roots and joints, three qian, boiled in water to remove foam, then dried. Gui Zhi two qian. Seven Xiong Ren, peeled and fried until yellow, then ground into a paste. Zhi Gan Cao one qian. Combine the above into a coarse powder, mix with almond paste evenly. Take one qian each time, with six fen of water, decoct until reduced to four fen, strain and take warm, at any time, based on sweating output, adjust dosage accordingly. If experiencing spontaneous sweating, it is not suitable for consumption.

Jin Fei Cao Powder
Treats wind injury with phlegm, dizziness and pain in the head, stiffness in the neck, alternating chills and fever, body aches, fullness in the chest, difficulty with phlegm and saliva, cough and wheezing, thick and sticky snot; also treats seasonal cold and epidemics with strong fever and aversion to wind.
Jing Jie four liang, Qian Hu three liang, Ma Huang without joints three liang, Xuan Fu Hua three liang, Zhi Gan Cao, Ban Xia soaked in ginger juice after washing seven times, Chi Shao each one liang.

Wheat Decoction Powder

This is used to treat children suffering from mixed colds, signs of shock, vomiting, intense heat, unrelieved exterior and interior symptoms, coarse breathing, flushed faces with spontaneous sweating, possible delirium, or silence with no sweating; also for widespread rash with itching, intermittent fevers, and symptoms of variola, residual toxins remaining, generalized edema, and cough with phlegm; or in cases of gradual seizures, convulsions in hands and feet, eyes looking upward, as well as for headaches caused by wind.

Ingredients:

  • Talc
  • Earth SKU (Dibone)
  • Red Peony
  • Gypsum
  • White Poria
  • Apricot Kernel
  • Stir-fried Lepidium
  • Ginseng, 7.5 grams each
  • Ephedra (remove the joints), 45 grams

Grind these into a powder, and for each dose, take 3 grams mixed with a decoction of wheat. This is suitable for infants with cold symptoms, having a cold body with a hot head, frequent sneezing and crying. Each dose should be administered in the wheat decoction.

Additionally, for another method, remove the Earth SKU and talc, and add Qianghuo and Chuanxiong, incorporating mint in the decoction for administration.[63p]
Xiao Qing Long Decoction is used to treat unrelieved exterior symptoms of excessive cold, with chills and fever, water retention under the heart, dry heaving, fever accompanied by cough, potential thirst or diarrhea, difficulty urinating, possible choking, and fullness in the lower abdomen with shortness of breath.

Ingredients:

  • Ephedra 7.5 grams
  • Red Peony Root 7.5 grams
  • Processed Pinellia 7.5 grams
  • Asarum 7.5 grams
  • Processed Dried Ginger 7.5 grams
  • Cinnamon 7.5 grams
  • Licorice 7.5 grams
  • Schisandra 15 grams

Grind the above into powder. Take 9 grams per dose, with one cup of water, simmer down to 70% and strain, adjusting as needed. For mild conditions, omit Ephedra and add flowering dogwood about the size of a ball, stir-fry until red. If there is choking, omit Ephedra and add 1.5 grams of processed Aconite. If there is difficulty urinating, add 30 grams of Poria. If there is shortness of breath, add blanched apricot kernels. If there is thirst, omit Pinellia and add the root of Trichosanthes.[64p]
Ren Shen Jing Jie San is a classic remedy used to treat body heat, phlegm cough, and obstruction in the chest, suitable for clearing phlegm and removing heat.

The ingredients are:

  • 0.25 taels of ginseng
  • 1 tael of schizonepeta flower
  • 2 qians of rhubarb

Grind the above ingredients into a fine powder, then decoct with water. Add 0.5 qian each of betel nut and aromatic wood powder, and a pinch of light powder; take after meals. If there is body heat and fever, it is advisable to use a cooling drink and omit the rhubarb. After three doses, wait one or two days before reintroducing rhubarb to promote thorough elimination for recovery. Be careful not to disturb the internal organs too hastily.

Jie Biao San (Release the Exterior Powder) is indicated for symptoms of wind-cold, cough with phlegm and wheezing, vomiting, diarrhea, palpitations with heat, and conditions manifesting both externally and internally.

The ingredients are:

  • Ma Huang (Ephedra)
  • Almonds (peeled and soaked)
  • 1 tael each of crimson poria and Chuanxiong (Szechuan lovage)
  • 0.75 tael each of Fang Feng (Siler) and Zhi Qiao (bitter orange) (cooked until lightly yellow)
  • 0.375 taels of licorice (half raw and half roasted)

Grind the above and use 2 qians at a time, boil with a cup of water, 2 slices of ginger, and one stalk of scallion, simmer until reduced to 70%, and take warm at any time. If there’s heat, add mint and decoct together.[65p]
Harmonizing Decoction treats children with colds caused by cold pathogens, causing strong heat and restlessness, nasal congestion with copious discharge, fright, spontaneous sweating, body aches, and rashes that may or may not have appeared. It can be taken by all.

Huangqin Powder
For treating cough in children. Use Huangqin in whatever amount, soak it in a child's urine for three days, then take it out, grind it to powder, and dry it. The powder is to be taken in small amounts, either one or half a qian, mixed with a little warm water, and taken after meals.

Maidong Decoction
Treats cough in children with strong heat and chest obstruction.
1 ounce Maidong, 0.5 ounce fresh ginger juice, 2 servings each of honey and clarified butter, 1 ounce peeled apricot kernels soaked in sweet almond soup.
First, boil Maidong and apricot kernels in 1 large cup of water until reduced to one-fourth. Grind in a mortar, strain to extract juice, then place into silverware. Next, add the ginger juice and simmer on low heat until thick, storing in porcelain. Each dose is mixed with half a teaspoon and taken with clear porridge, three times a day and once at night, adjusting dosage according to the child's size.

Reduces phlegm and stops coughing.

Xixin Wuweizi Decoction (from "Zhengzhi Zhuansheng") for treating lung meridian deficiency, weak stomach qi, potential exposure to wind pathogens, or stagnant cold with fluid retention, cough that worsens with reliance, difficulty in lying down comfortably, fullness in the chest with shortness of breath, dry retching causing heat cough, expectoration of phlegm or spittle, dizziness in the head, heaviness in the body, difficulty in speaking, pain radiating to the chest and ribs—suitable to take regardless of duration.

Baimu Decoction for infants under a hundred days with cough and phlegm.

The "Golden Round" from "Qiyou Liangfang" treats chronic coughs, coarse breathing with excess phlegm, mouth sores, and eye heat; it is used after dispersing. Ingredients include:

  • 1 part ginseng
  • 1 part white poria
  • 1 part polygala root (remove heart)
  • 1 part Chinese yam
  • 1 part cinnabar
  • 1 part bright gastrodia
  • 1 part stone calamus
  • 1 part chuanxiong
  • 1 part honey-fried licorice
  • 2 qian tian nanxing (prepared)
  • a drop of fresh ginger juice
  • a bit of musk

Grind these into a fine powder, and mix with honey to form pellets the size of jujubes. Take one pellet with peppermint soup.

The "Baolong Pill" from "Quanyu Xinjian" treats children with wind-phlegm, heat toxins, and stagnation, cooling the heart and calming fright. Ingredients include:

  • 1 liang of ox gall and tian nanxing
  • 10 pieces of gold foil
  • 1.5 qian of cinnabar
  • 1 part dragon brain
  • 1 part musk

Grind these into a powder, form into balls the size of lotus seeds with honey. Take one ball with bamboo leaf soup.

The "Four Substance Decoction" from "Waicai Xiaopin" treats sudden cough in children from ten days to fifty days, causing vomiting, with no rest day or night. Ingredients include:

  • 3 fen of platycodon
  • 3 fen of aster
  • 1 fen of honey-fried licorice
  • 7 fen of ophiopogon

Prepare this by boiling in one liter of water until reduced to six parts, strain, and divide into five doses, taking as needed. "Qianjin" has cinnamon heart but no platycodon; use two liters of water, boil down to one liter. Use cotton to touch the soup, letting it drip into the child's mouth four to five times throughout the day, as appropriate during breastfeeding.[74p]
Xionghuang ointment for treating coughs in children under three:

Take seven pieces of Banxia, soak them in a child's urine overnight, slice them, and dry them into powder. One over ten of Xionghuang, finely ground. Seven almonds, with skin and tips removed.

Mix well in a container with half an ounce of fresh ginger juice and half an ounce of honey, then place the medicinal powder inside and cook in a decoction, stirring with willow twigs to create a paste. Each dose is to be applied the size of a soap piece to the nipple for the child to suck, or mixed with glutinous rice drink to ingest.

Baolong Pill: Used for coughs in children with heat in the spleen and stomach.

Use four ounces of Nanzhing, if there are no cow gallbladders, simply grind and fry it until cooked. One ounce of Tianzhuhuang. Water-fried Xionghuang and separate ground cinnabar, each half an ounce. One dime of musk, also ground separately.

These are ground into a fine powder, combined with cooked licorice paste, and made into pills the size of soap pods dissolved in warm water. For infants, divide each pill into three or four doses; for five-year-olds, one or two pills.

Sanhuang Pill: Used for coughs due to heat with sores in the mouth and eyes, and firm stools.

Equal parts of Huanglian, Huangqin, and Da Huang, processed.[75p]
The following is the English translation of the provided Classical Chinese text:

The formula is finalized: make pills the size of a tung seed, adjusting the quantity according to the child's size, and take with boiling water.

Jinhua Powder (from "General Principles of Health") treats cough in infants. Ingredients: half a tael of turmeric, half a tael of windbreak herb (excluding the leaves and branches), one fen each of pinellia and croton seeds, and one block of soapberry. Boil these ingredients in one liter of water in a silver container until the water evaporates; discard the croton seeds and soapberry. Clean the other three ingredients separately with warm water, dry, and powder finely. For infants, give one character's worth; for those aged two to three, give half a qian; for those aged four to five and above, give one qian, mixed in mint honey water. There are no restrictions on when to administer.

Apricot Seed Decoction (from "Sacred Effective Formulas") treats children's cough with little sound. Ingredients: soak the apricot seeds, remove the skin and tip, and grind them in one bowl of water; filter to obtain two taels of juice. Combine with one heaping paired unit of butter and honey. First, boil the apricot juice in a kettle and reduce by half, then add the butter and honey, and boil for another twenty times. After that, add one fen each of fritillaria and aster powders and half a fen of licorice powder, and continue boiling while stirring until thickened, then store in a ceramic container. Each dose is taken with half a qian of thin rice gruel, three times during the day and once at night. Adjust the dosage according to the child's size until the cough stops.

Another formula: half a tael of fritillaria, fine-ground cow bile one qian, and one fen of roasted licorice. Mash and sift these ingredients into a powder. For each dose, mix half a qian with warm water and take three to four times a day, adjusting the dosage according to the child's size.

Another formula.[76p]
Mai Men Dong Decoction:
To the heart, add 1 fen of Mai Men Dong, 1 fen of blanched apricot kernels (remove the skin), roast and yellow steeped wheat, prepared licorice, 1 fen of fried Fritillaria bulb, and 1 fen of winter flower. Remove soil from the 紫菀 (Aster tataricus), using half a Liang.
Crush the above medicines and sieve finely to make a powder. Each dose is mixed with half a Qian of milk and taken three to four times a day, adjusting according to the child's size.

Another Prescription:
1 Liang of apricot kernels, the pointed double kernals (remove the skin), grind with 1 medium cup of water to extract juice; half a Liang of 紫菀 powder.
Combine the apricot juice and 紫菀 powder with 1 plate of honey and cook until it turns into a paste. Each dose should be mixed with congee and taken with half a teaspoon, adjusting according to the size of the child.

Chen Ju Pi Powder:
For treating children's cough and rendering a嗄嗄 sound in the throat.
Steep aged orange peel and remove the white part; soak apricot kernels in water and remove skin, roast and make yellow; prepare licorice when slightly red and softened; roast sweet licorice till slightly purple; and finely chopped white mulberry root, all 1 fen each.
Crush the above medicines and sieve coarsely for powder. Each dose is 1 Qian, boiled with 1 small cup of water until reduced to 5 parts, strained, and set aside to cool, adjusting for the size of the child.

Radish Seed Powder:
For treating children's cough, wheezing, and producing a嗄嗄 sound.
Roasted radish seeds, 1 fen; prepare 麻黄 (Ephedra sinica) by removing the root nodules; a bundle of lampwick; 10 pieces of soap pods (remove the skin); half a fen of slightly roasted licorice.
Crush the above medicines and sieve coarsely for powder. Each dose is 1 Qian, boiled with 1 small cup of water until reduced to 5 parts, strained and taken warm without time restriction, adjusting according to the size of the child.[77p]
Cicada Shell Powder: Treats children with phlegm blockage in the chest, coughing, and difficulty in swallowing, often making sounds like "ya" and "ge." Lightly fry cicada shells, wash Pinellia in a decoction seven times to remove slipperiness, and use half a tael each of roasted licorice and prepared bitter pokeweed. Soak half a tael each of platycodon and aged tangerine peel in a soup to remove the white and roast. Grind the above ingredients into a fine powder, and take it with fresh ginger porridge, adjusting to one spoonful, and for children three years old and above, add half a coin.

Zhimu Decoction: Treats coughing with nasal congestion, wheezing, phlegm sounds, fever, and aversion to wind. Use half a tael each of Anemarrhena and licorice, and three qian each of Fritillaria, Qianghuo, talc ground separately, rhubarb, and wheat. Prepare Ma Huang by soaking it in soup to remove foam and roast, as well as one and a half qian each of bitter lepidium and chebula fruit flesh, and two qian of peppermint after removing the stems. Chew the above ingredients, take two qian each time with one cup of water, two slices of ginger, decoct until reduced to seven portions, and take warm at any time.

Xionghuang Powder: For acute and chronic fright wind, nasal congestion with excess phlegm, and conditions caused by damp invasion, with unregulated sweating and either cool or hot sensations, causing irritability when sitting or lying down. Use two and a half qian of realgar, half a tael each of white peony, processed Aconitum carmichaelii with skin and belly removed, processed Aconitum sinomontanum with skin removed, and Tianma, and three qian of Chuanxiong. Excluding realgar, grind the other five ingredients well and mix with realgar into a powder. For fright wind with phlegm obstruction, take half a coin or one coin each time, using ginger juice and herbal tea for adjustment; for inducing sweating, boil water, ginger, scallions, and peppermint together, and take three doses for effect.[78p]
Ruyi Ointment: Treats phlegm, wheezing, and persistent coughing, suitable for both hot and cold conditions.
Preparation of Banxia and Nanshan: Each of these two ingredients weighs 1.5 taels. Grind the two together into a powder, mix with fresh ginger juice, and shape into small cakes the size of coins. Dry them slowly over low heat, then grind into a powder again. Repeat the process with ginger juice two more times, then dry and grind into powder again. Form into pill-sized balls with honey, about the size of a chestnut, taking 1 to 2 pills each time with ginger honey soup, and can be taken at any time. If there is heat, take with mint soup.

Xionghuang Dan: Treats children with cough and shortness of breath, heart and chest discomfort, clears heat and eliminates toxins.
Ingredients: 1 qian each of xionghuang (realgar) and zhushaba (cinnabar), ground separately; 14 pieces of apricot kernels, roasted; 7 pieces of ba dou (croton seed); 21 pieces of faint soybeans.
For the above ingredients, use half a cup of rice vinegar, a piece of dried ginger the size of a finger tip, boil until dry, and grind into a paste. One inch of soapwort is roasted until charred; remove the seeds and skin. Combine this with 1 fen of ox gall, and mix with xionghuang, zhushaba, and apricot paste, grinding finely to mix. Form into pills the size of sesame seeds, giving 5 pills for a one-year-old, 7 for a stronger child, and 10 for a two-year-old, taken with light ginger soup.[79p]
Baimu Wan (from "Yujue")
Treats nasal congestion in children.
Baimu, Tian Nansheng, ginger juice, Ren Shen, Fu Ling, honey-fried licorice, and Bai Fu Zi, all in equal parts. Use seven pieces of soap pod (Zao Jiao), roast, and grind into a fine powder. Mix with honey to form pills the size of a small bean. Take five to seven pills each time, swallowed with peppermint tea.

You Gun Wan (from "Zhengzhi Zhunjian")
Treats nasal congestion in children and accumulations of parasites.
Lei Wan, Wu Ling Zhi, each one part, fifteen seeds of Ba Dou (ban beans), oil removed. Grind into a fine powder, shape into pills, each time taking three to five pills, treated with sesame oil and swallowed with well water.

Wu Ling San (from "Quan You Xin Jian")
Treats nasal congestion in children and dispels wind and phlegm.
Ze Xie, Zhu Ling, Bai Fu Ling, Bai Zhu, and Guan Gui, all in equal parts. Grind into a fine powder, taking ten grams each time, mixed with warm water, at any time.[80p]
Kuan Qi Drink
Treats the same as above.
Soak the husked water to remove the fibrous part, lightly roast the bran until slightly yellow. Use one tael each of bitter orange fruit. Remove the roots of ginseng; use half a tael of the roasted licorice. Grind the above ingredients into a fine powder, take half a qian to one qian with clear soup at any time.

Kuan Re Drink
Treats the same as above.
One tael of rhubarb, seven and a half qian of powdered licorice, two and a half qian of yuanming powder, one tael of bitter orange fruit (remove the fibrous part) sliced, fifteen seeds of castor bean (make into two pieces, remove the shell and membrane heart, both roasted until the bitter orange fruit is slightly yellow), remove the castor bean.
Grind the rhubarb, powdered licorice, and bitter orange fruit into a fine powder, add the yuanming powder, then mix well in a mortar. Take half a qian to one qian at any time. For children, reduce the dose and use ginger honey soup or mint soup.

Ban Xia Pill
Treats the same as above.
Use two taels of fresh ban xia, one tael each of red poria (remove skin) and bitter orange fruit, two and a half qian of wind-processed (stone potassium) nitrate.
Grind the first three ingredients into a fine powder, mix with the stone potassium nitrate in a mortar using fresh ginger juice to make dough with glutinous rice flour into pills the size of soybeans. Take thirty to fifty pills, washed down with light ginger soup before sleeping. For children, make the pills the size of millet.[81p]
Liu Wanshu's Formula for Moistening the Lungs
For treating children's phlegm heat, cough, and wheezing that long remains untreated:
One gourd seed, remove the seeds and use the pulp. Grind it into a powder, mix with cold food flour to form a paste, roast until yellow, then powder. Take one qian with warm water mixed with lactose, three times a day, stop when effective.

Neijin Pill (from "Zhengzhi Zhunspring")
For treating children's cough (with nasal obstruction):
Chicken inner golden (ji neijin), finely ground and whisked with water, exposed for three days for usage. Fresh half summer and Yanhusuo in equal parts. Grind into powder, mix with jujube flesh to form small bean-sized pills. For children aged one year, take three to four pills in light bulb thread soup.

Jishi Family Inherited Remedy for Coughing
Tianzhuhuang and clam powder, stir-fried.
Grind evenly in equal parts, mix with honey and apply to the head as well as consume.

Brain Powder
For treating persistent cough in children from cold, also addressing Qi stagnation.
One part rhubarb, two qian turmeric.
First, boil with pig's tooth soapwort for a while, slice, dry, and grind into powder. Then add a little powdered brain, and grind together until uniform. Take one character sized dose, mixed with sugar water; adjust dosage based on the child's build.[82p]
Nine Treasures Decoction: Treats children's cough caused by lung cold invasion; must disperse the surface, but do not use cough medicine. Ingredients: 4.5g Ephedra (without nodes), 4.5g Peppermint, 4.5g Large abdominal skin, 4.5g Perilla leaves, 7.5g Aged tangerine peel, 7.5g Almond (peeled and ground), 7.5g Mulberry bark (roasted), 7.5g Cinnamon, 7.5g Bitter orange peel, 4.5g Licorice (roasted). Grind these together. Take 6g with decocted ginger and black plum. For cold syndromes, omit peppermint. For heat syndromes, omit aged tangerine peel and cinnamon.

Hua Gai Powder: Treats lung cold stagnation, cough with shortness of breath, chest fullness, tightness in the neck and back, heavy voice, nasal congestion, dizziness, and phlegm obstruction. Ingredients: 4.5g Ephedra (without nodes), 4.5g Perilla seeds (stir-fried), 4.5g Mulberry bark (honey-roasted), 4.5g Almond (peeled and stir-fried), 4.5g Red Poria, 4.5g Aged tangerine peel (white part removed), 6g Licorice (roasted). Grind these together. Take 6g with half a cup of water, simmer until reduced to one third, strain, adjust dosage based on size, and take warm after meals.

Gua Lou Powder [from the Book of Holy Benefits]: Treats children's persistent cough and restlessness. Ingredients: 1 Gourd fruit (remove seeds if hot), mix with 1 liter of children's urine, grind and strain to extract the juice; 50g Suet; 3g Fresh licorice powdered; 100g Honey. Combine these ingredients in a silver pot and simmer over low heat until syrupy. For each dose, mix with half a cup of rice gruel, taken four to five times a day, adjusting for the child's size.[83p]
Buhui Mu San

For treating prolonged coughs in children: Use Buhui wood, burned with cow dung until it turns red. Prepare Fritillaria bulbs until slightly yellow, and roast licorice until slightly red; each of these ingredients should weigh half a tael. Grind the above ingredients into a coarse powder. For each dose, take one qian (a small weight), mix it in a small cup of freshly drawn water, and add one or two drops of raw oil. Stir well, boil until reduced by half, strain out the residue, and divide into two warm doses to be taken four times a day, adjusting the amount according to the child's size.

Sang Bai Pi Jiang

For treating prolonged coughs in children and for phlegm-heat with blood: Use five pieces of the white bark of mulberry roots, cut the white lung of a white dog, add licorice, Poria, Cimicifuga, and Fritillaria, each two fen (a smaller weight), along with peony, roasted apricot kernels, each ten fen, cut four fen of the white bark of plum roots, and add six fen each of Radix Stellariae and Ophiopogon, eleven fen of Scutellaria, eight fen of green bamboo skin, and one sheng (a volume measure) each of honey and Rehmannia juice.

Combine all these with ten sheng of water, boil until reduced to three sheng, strain out the residue, then add apricot paste, Rehmannia juice, and honey, simmering gently while stirring continuously until reduced to two sheng and three ge (a smaller volume measure). For children aged two to three years, give one ge warm, three times a day, and at night give three ge.[84p]
Zhi Mu Powder: Used for treating children with a persistent cough, phlegm, and wheezing. Ingredients: Zhi Mu (Anemarrhena), Chuan Bei Mu (Fritillaria), Chai Hu (Bupleurum), roasted Huang Qi (Astragalus), cleaned Zi Wan (Aster), Ma Dou Ling (Aristolochia), peeled and ground Xing Ren (Apricot), Bai Zhu (Alisma), dried Sāng Bái Pí (Mulberry bark), ground Bai Fan (Alum), and equal portions of Dong Hua (winter flower).

The above should be finely powdered. Each dose is one qian, mixed with seven fen of water, boiled for three fen, strained and taken frequently; alternatively, use fresh ginger juice, cooked into a paste and formed into pills, taking five to seven pills with ginger soup.

Bei Mu Powder: Used for treating children with a persistent cough and urgency of breath. Ingredients: Bèi Mǔ (Fritillaria), roasted Xing Ren (Apricot), Mai Dong (Ophiopogon), equal portions of Dong Hua (winter flower), and half a liang of Zi Wan (Aster).

The above should be ground to powder and mixed with milk to take half a qian.

Complete Apricot Pill: Used for treating cough after convulsions in children.[85p]
Almonds peeled and pointed, sweet gentian, Chinese yam, and peeled Aristolochia, grind the above into a powder and make small pills the size of a mung bean using honey. Take ten pills each time, swallowing them with cooked water of Ophiopogon. Mr. Mao also had this recipe for cough treatment, stating that they have mutual linkages that cannot be removed, hence both should be preserved.

Yunqi Powder treats similarly as above.

Get rid of the fibrous head of Platycodon, wash it clean, five liang; two liang of licorice; one liang each of crushed cardamom, washed aromatic ginger, aged tangerine peel; one fen of white ginger. Grind the above into a fine powder, taking half a qian each time, using boiled broth of frost-matured papaya for mixing; if not available, use boiled broth of perilla with salt.

Huo Xiang Powder [same as in "Total Microcosm of Health"] treats cough due to disharmony of lung and stomach not caused by wind or cold. Take twenty-one Huo Xiang leaves, one piece of bitter orange peel (removing the seeds), wrap it in wet paper and steam it until cooked, and one piece of clam powder about the size of the orange peel. Grind the above into a fine powder, and for infants, take a small amount—half a qian for those two to three years old—mix it in honey water to take, no more than two or three doses for safety. For larger children, adjust accordingly without specific timing.

Ginger Decoction treats children's coughs.

One liang of fresh ginger, six qian of dried ginger, one fen of cassia heart, four qian of roasted licorice, one liang of peeled and stir-fried almonds; four liang each of winter flowers and purple aster. Grind the above into a powder, mix one liang of honey with the medicine, simmer with low heat until syrupy, adjusting the quantity to the child's preference for dissolving and swallowing. For infants around a hundred days old, the size of a jujube pit, take three times daily for significant effect.[86p]

Ginseng and Pinellia Decoction: Treats children's phlegm counterflow and persistent cough.
Ingredients:

  • Ginseng
  • Pinellia, each half a tael

    Kuan Fei San: Treats wind obstructing phlegm in children, causing severe cough, shortness of breath, high fever, red cheeks, delirium, vomiting, facial swelling, and decreased appetite.

Ingredients:

  • 5 taels of silkworms, cleaned and dried
  • 3 taels of Corydalis

Grind the above into a powder. For each dose, take a character (a small amount) or half a cash, mix with warm thin juice, and take at any time. For infants, mix half a character with breast milk.

Zao Jia Chi Tang: Treats cough in children.

Ingredients:

Wu Ling Zhi Wan: Treats chronic cough that leads to weakness, fear of developing malnourishment.

Ingredients:

  • 1 piece of toad head, fried in fat until yellow
  • Wu Ling Zhi, cleaned of sand and soil
  • Lightly toasted cicada shells
  • Half tael each of winter jasmine flower and blue indigo, ground
  • 1/10 tael each of realgar, ground and mixed with water

Mix all ingredients well and form into pills the size of millet grains. For each dose, take ten pills with prepared ginseng soup, after meals.

Ren Shen Xi Jiao San: Treats seasonal cold obstruction causing cough with reverse phlegm, wheezing, anxiety, and wind-heat symptoms.

Ingredients:

  • 8 qian of Qian Hu
  • 3 qian each of ginseng and fried licorice
  • 5 qian each of Platycodon and almonds, soaked, peeled, and dried

Grind the first four ingredients together, mix in the almond powder, sift through a coarse sieve. For each dose, take 2 qian, boil with one cup of water until reduced by 30%, strain, warm, and take after meals.[88p]
Mercury and Pinellia Pill: Treats phlegm and coughing due to cold.
Combine honey-fried Trichosanthes root and Tian Nan Xing decoction, wash Pinellia seven times, and roast dried ginger; each ingredient weighs half a tael. Grind these into a fine powder. Mix with fresh ginger juice to form pills the size of a sesame seed, coated with red mercury. Take ten pills with ginger decoction, at any time.

Jade Pearl Pill: Treats various types of phlegm-related coughing.
Use one tael of Pinellia, washed seven times, and one part of nitre. Grind into a fine powder, form into pills the size of a sesame seed, and take three to five pills with ginger decoction, at any time.

Beech Honeycomb Pill: Treats deficiency and cold in the lungs and stomach, cough, wheezing, fullness, nausea, and lack of appetite.
One gecko (weighing four qian), fried honeycomb, fried cicada shell (with dirt removed), Mu Xiang, cloves, ginseng, Rehmannia, Ma Huang (roots removed), Aristolochia fructus, Wu Bei Zi (dusted of insects), each two qian; North Schisandra, fritillaria (heart removed and roasted), apricot kernels (soaked in young boy's urine for two nights, peeled, and then roasted), half a tael of winter cress flowers (stems removed). Grind all into a fine powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of a broad bean, and take twenty to thirty pills with ginger decoction three to four times a day after meals.[89p]
Almond Paste: Treats cough in children where sound is absent. Take one tael of almonds, soak in soup to remove the skin, tips, and double almond kernels. Use one jar of water to squeeze out the juice. Take half a tael of purple aster, wash away the soil and grind to a fine powder. Mix the purple aster powder into the almond juice, add one heaping spoon of honey, and simmer into a paste. Take half a teaspoon each time, diluted in clear congee, and can be taken at any time.

Gold Dust: Treats coughs due to wind-phlegm, with red cheeks and excessive phlegm, breathlessness, vomiting, and retention of fluids, along with reduced milk intake. Use one tael of unspooled silkworms, half a tael of roasted licorice root, and one point of Corydalis. Grind into fine powder. Take a pinch each time, diluted with juice. For infants, dilute with half a character's worth of milk after meals.

Calm Breathing Decoction: Treats wind damage, lung qi deficiency, wheezing, and coughing. Use one and a half taels of white mulberry bark, half a tael of white poria, roasted unspooled silkworms, white atractylodes, with the skin and tips of the almonds removed and ground in, half tael each of platycodon and dried tangerine peel, and one point each of licorice and ginseng (with the roots removed). Grind to a fine powder. Take one qian, add one cup of water, three slices of ginger, and two almonds, and boil down to six parts. Strain and take warm at intervals.[90p]
This text provides a formula for treating various types of coughs, detailing specific herbs and ingredients to use based on the characteristics of the cough. It includes instructions on preparation and dosage for each type, emphasizing the efficacy of the remedies. Here's the translated English text:

This text outlines remedies for sixteen types of cough.

For general coughs: Use one tael each of Ejiao, fried Ma Dou Ling, roasted herbs, and Ban Xia soaked in ginger juice for three days, along with peeled apricot kernels. Combine with half a tael of ginseng and grind. Take two qian after meals, with soup prepared in advance.

For heart cough, with a flushed face or sweating, add dried Kudzu.

For liver cough, with tears in the eyes, add one dried plum and fourteen grains of glutinous rice.

For wheezing cough, with a sound like a saw, add two pieces of Ban Xia.

For spleen cough, with loss of appetite or nausea, add two slices of raw ginger.

For stomach cough, with reverse stomach acid, add clam powder.

For gallbladder cough, causing sleeplessness, use half a tael of medicine mixed with clear tea.

For lung cough, with urgent shortness of breath, add mulberry root.

For diaphragm cough, producing phlegm in round lumps, mix with fresh ginger juice.

For fatigue cough, add powdered Qin Jiao.

For cold cough, worsening at night, add three inches of green onion.

For blood cough, frequent and persistent, add powdered Angelica and dates.

For sudden cough, with thick and sticky phlegm, add dried plum and fresh ginger.

For postpartum cough, with back pain, add three inches of licorice and a small amount of yellow wax.

For qi cough, with abdominal pain and distension, add green skin (of fruits).

For kidney cough, with intermittent sounds, add Astragalus and white candy.

The above sixteen types of cough, when treated according to these methods, will show effective results.[91p]
Gui Pi Decoction
For treating children's depression and qi stagnation causing wheezing.
Ingredients:

  • Ginseng, Astragalus, Poria, Licorice, Fried Atractylodes, Polygala, Sour Jujube Seed, Longan Fruit, Angelica (each 3 grams)
  • Wood Fragrance (2.5 grams)
  • Additionally, add Chai Hu and Gardenia for decoction.

Yang Wei Decoction
For treating children's food stagnation causing wheezing.
Ingredients:

  • Ginseng, Magnolia Bark, Atractylodes, Prepared Pinellia, Agastache, Grass Fruit Seed, Poria (each 15 grams)
  • Honey-fried Licorice, Tangerine Peel (each 7.5 grams)
  • Take 6-9 grams each time, add a little Wood Fragrance, and decoct with water.

Wu Lin Powder
For treating hidden heat in the lungs, causing inability to produce water and wheezing.
Ingredients:

  • Red Poria, Red Peony (each 2.5 grams)
  • Fried Gardenia, Angelica (each 1.5 grams)
  • Licorice (1 gram)
  • Use 10 strands of lampwick for decoction.

Huang Qin Qing Fei Powder
For treating the same conditions as above.
Ingredients:

  • Huang Qin (3 grams)
  • One Gardenia, broken
  • Decoct with water for consumption. If ineffective, add 20 seeds of fermented soybeans.

Zi Shen Pill
For treating children's spleen and lung accumulation of heat causing wheezing.
Ingredients:

  • Fried Huang Bo, scorched (9 grams)
  • Zhimu (6 grams)
  • Cinnamon (2.5 grams)
  • Grind all into powder, form into pills the size of a tung seed, taking 20-30 pills each time with hot boiled water before meals.

Si Shun Qing Liang Drink
For treating children's heat accumulation causing upper qi to wheeze.
Ingredients:

  • Red Peony, Angelica, Licorice, Rhubarb (equal parts) [92p]
    Here is the translation:

The above formula is to be taken in one qian, boiled with water to make two doses.

Bā Wèi Dì Huáng Wán (Eight Ingredient Rehmannia Pill) is used to treat spleen and stomach deficiency cold, with umbilical protrusion, abdominal distension, and wheezing.

  • Shú Dì Huáng (Prepared Rehmannia): 8 qian
  • Shān Zhū Yù Ròu (Cornelian Cherry Fruit) and Dried Shān Yào (Chinese Yam): each 4 qian
  • Wǔ Wèi (Five Flavor Fruit), Ròu Guì (Cinnamon), Zé Xiè (Alisma), Mǔ Dān Pí (Peony Bark), and Bái Fú Líng (Poria): each 3 qian.

Grind these into a powder, mix with Rehmannia syrup and add rice paste, form into pills the size of a tongzi (large nut), take a few pills with warm water on an empty stomach.

Jiā Jiǎn Shèn Qì Wán (Modified Kidney Qi Pill) from the "Jīn Guì" prescription is used to treat spleen and kidney deficiency cold, unable to retain fluids, with symptoms of bloating and wheezing.

  • Shú Dì Huáng: 8 liang
  • Dried Shān Yào and Shān Zhū Yù: each 4 liang
  • Zé Xiè, Bái Fú Líng, Mǔ Dān Pí: each 3 liang
  • Ròu Guì, Fù Zǐ (Prepared Aconite), Chē Qián Zǐ (Plantago Seed) stir-fried, and Niú Xī (Achyranthes root) slightly stir-fried: each 1 liang.

Grind these into powder separately, mix with rice paste to form small bean-sized pills, take 30 to 40 pills on an empty stomach, before meals with clear soup.

Mǎ Tōng Sù Lì Wán (Horse Gather Millet Pill) from “Wèi Shēng Zǒng Wēi” is used to treat children with wheezing, shoulder breath inversion, pain below the ribs, alternating chills and fevers, inability to take milk or food, gradually leading to emaciation.

  • Mǎ Tōng Zhōng Sù Lì: 3 fen
  • Apricot kernel soaked and peeled: ½ liang
  • Zǐ Wàn (Aster Root) and Xì Xīn (Asarum): each ½ liang
  • Shí Gāo (Gypsum) and Qín Jiāo (Gentian) soaked in half summer tea 7 times; Bái Fú Líng and Wǔ Wèi Zǐ (Schisandra): each 1 fen.

Grind these into a powder, refine with honey into small bean-sized pills, take ten pills with ginger soup, three times a day, increasing to twenty pills at any time.[93p]
Jiang Zhu Dan: Treats phlegm, saliva, and wheezing fullness.
Nan Xing Pao: Ban Xia decoction to wash away slipperiness.
Hua Shi: Each two taels.
Ku Bai Fan: Two halves.
Qian Bai Shuang: One part.
The above is finely powdered, mixed into a paste and formed into pills the size of millet seeds, coated with vermilion. Take ten pills at a time, swallow with ginger soup, after meals and before lying down.

Bi Yu Wan: Treats phlegm cough, asthma, chest fullness, reduced appetite, restless sleep, and irritability with heat.
Qing Dai, Sheng Fan, Sheng Nan Xing, Hua Shi: each two qian five fen.
Ba Dou: forty-nine seeds, remove the shell and the inner membrane, keep the oil, finely grind in a mortar.
Qing Fen: fifteen slips.
Quan Xie: fifteen tails, detoxified.
Except for Qing Fen and Ba Dou, the remaining five flavors should be sun-dried or baked into powder, combined in the mortar with the previous two flavors. Mix ginger juice with glutinous rice flour to form a paste, shape into pills the size of millet, take seven to nine pills, or eleven pills, swallowed with light ginger soup on an empty stomach. For those with extreme heat, take with peppermint soup, regardless of time.[94p]
Kanli Decoction: Treats weakness with light daytime wheezing and heavier nighttime symptoms, reduced appetite and a foggy mind. Ingredients include: 1 qian of Piper longum, Acorus tatarinowii; 2 qian each of Atractylodes macrocephala, Poria cocos, and Alpinia oxyphylla; 4 qian each of roasted honey, and processed Pinellia ternata; and 4 qian of roasted Perilla seeds, crushed. Grind the latter and use 2 qian with one cup of water to decoct until reduced by two-thirds. Take warm at any time.

Apricot Kernel Decoction (from "Shenghui Fang"): Treats children’s cough, with restlessness and coarse breathing. Ingredients are: 1 liang of apricot kernels (peeled and double-kernel removed, slightly roasted), 1 liang of Asparagus cochinchinensis (heart removed), 1 liang of cold food flour, 1 guo each of honey and rendered fat, and 0.5 liang of fritillaria (fried). Mix with 1 large cup of raw Rehmannia juice. Decoct fritillaria and Asparagus until reduced to one-tenth; then strain the juice, mix it with the apricot paste, cook until it reaches the consistency of thin syrup. Each dose is mixed with warm water, taken as half a qian, adjusting based on the child's size.

Eight Flavor Regulating Pills (from "Zheng Zhi Zhun Sheng"): Treats children with disharmony of heart and lungs, rapid and urgent pulse, difficulty in breath rising and falling, fullness and pressure in the middle abdomen, chest distress, irritability when sitting or lying down, malaise, and lack of appetite. Ingredients are equal parts: ginseng, roasted licorice, Atractylodes macrocephala, dried ginger, stir-fried bitter orange, Poria cocos, Schisandra, and Mulberry root. Grind all into fine powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of a small finger. Each dose is one pill, taken with five grains of fermented soybeans and one small cup of water, decocted until half the soybeans dissolve, taken orally at any time.[95p]
Pingqi San
Used to treat children with disharmonious qi, resolve wheezing, and replenish vitality for those with weak appetites.
Ingredients: Ginseng, white poria, lily bulb, roasted licorice, fried white atractylodes, and platycodon, all in equal parts.
Grind the six ingredients into a powder. Take 3 grams with 240 ml of water and a small amount of fresh ginger, decoct until reduced to 120 ml, and consume warm.

Buzhong Yiqi Tang
For similar indications as above.
Ingredients: 3 grams of angelica, 6 grams of ginseng, 6 grams of astragalus, 5 grams each of white atractylodes, licorice, and dried tangerine peel, and 0.6 grams each of schisandra and bupleurum.
Crush the ingredients, assess the required amount of water depending on the illness, strain out the residue, and take slightly warm before meals.

Sheng Bai Wan
Used to treat children with phlegm and mucus obstructions, leading to cough and wheezing.
Ingredients: 15 grams of white peony, 15 grams of fresh rhizome, and 30 grams of pinellia.
Grind the ingredients into a powder, mix with fresh ginger juice to form balls the size of mung beans. Take 20 to 30 balls with ginger soup, adjusting the quantity based on the child's size.

Zhi Shi Tang
Indicated for colds and wind-heat, chest fullness, shortness of breath, unproductive cough, and phlegm after heavy eating.
Ingredients: 15 grams of bitter orange (peeled and chopped), 15 grams of red poria (peeled), 6 grams of licorice, and 3 grams of pinellia.
Decoct the ingredients, strain, and then further dry them. For platycodon, use 22.5 grams, chop and fry until slightly toasted.
Take 6 grams of the mixture with 240 ml of water and 3 slices of ginger, decoct to about 120 ml and take at any time.[96p]
Qing Wei San (from "Introduction to Medicine")
For treating children who overeat rich foods, causing accumulation of heat in the spleen and stomach leading to wheezing.
Ingredients: 5 grams of Sheng Ma, 3 grams each of Sheng Di Huang, Mu Dan Pi, and Chuan Huang Lian (stir-fried), and 3 grams of Dang Gui.
Preparation: Boil with water to administer.

Da Xiao Xiong Zhu Hua Tan Ding Chuan Wan (from "Xue's Medical Cases")
For treating children who develop wheezing from fright, affecting the heart and lungs, presenting with acute mouth opening, anxiety, and lethargy.
Ingredients: 1 gram each of Xiong Huang and Zhu Sha, ground; 2.5 grams each of Chan Tui, Quan Xie (stir-fried), Di Long, Bai Jiang Can, Tian Nan Xing, and Bai Fu Zi (processed); 0.5 grams of Qing Fen.
Preparation: Grind all into a fine powder, form into pills the size of sesame seeds, take 30 pills with mint tea after meals.

Tian Ma Ding Chuan Yin (from "Principles of Diagnosis and Treatment")
For treating children's wheezing and cough due to fright.
Ingredients: Equal parts of Tian Ma, Fang Feng, Qiang Huo, Gan Cao, Ren Shen, Ju Ge, Bai Zhu, Chuan Xiong, and Ban Xia Qu.
Preparation: Finely grind, take 2 grams mixed with one cup of water, add 14 Mai Men Dong pieces, boil until reduced to 70%. Take after meals. If there is heat, remove Bai Zhu and add Shao Yao and Zhi Ke.[97p]
Zisu Drink: Treats lung conditions caused by wind and cold, with symptoms of wheezing and phlegm cough. Ingredients: Zisu leaves, mulberry bark, green peel, five-flavor fruit, apricot kernels, ephedra, honey-fried licorice, and dried tangerine peel, each two parts; ginseng and pinellia, each three parts. For preparation, add three slices of ginger, boil in water, and take warm.

Ephedra and Apricot Kernel Licorice Gypsum Decoction: Treats conditions after sweating due to a cold, where one cannot switch to Gui Zhi Decoction, experiences sweating but without high fever; also treats wheezing after purging. Ingredients: Two taels of ephedra (soak and remove the yellow juice then dry), twenty-five apricot kernels, four taels of gypsum (ground), and one tael of honey-fried licorice. Grind the above into a fine powder, take two qian (a measure), mix with a small cup of water, boil down to six parts, strain, and take warm.

Minor Blue Dragon Decoction with Gypsum: Treats pediatric lung distension, with coughing and shortness of breath, restlessness and wheezing, with a floating pulse, indicating water accumulation below the heart. Ingredients: Three taels of ephedra (remove the joints); four taels from "Qianjin"; two taels of gypsum; three taels each of peony, cinnamon twig, and asarum; two taels each from "Qianjin" of honey-fried licorice and dried ginger; half sheng (a volume measure) of pinellia, and half sheng of five-flavor fruit, as well as one sheng from "Qianjin". For preparation, chop the nine ingredients, boil with ten dou (a large volume measure) of water, reduce by one sheng, skim off the foam, add other ingredients, boil until three sheng remain, strain. For strong patients, take one sheng, reduce for weak patients, taking three times a day; for children, take four doses.[98p]
Gourd decoction for the Jishi formula: Treats children suffering from cold injury, wheezing, and excessive saliva.

One large gourd, lid opened;
One part of ejiao, half a tael of rock sugar.

Take these two ingredients and place them inside the gourd, sealing it with the lid. Paste white paper over it, then steam it in a rice steamer twice. Pour it out and administer according to the child's size, varying the dosage as needed.

Pearl powder: Treats children's wheezing and excess saliva.

Powdered pearl, half a penny of fresh rhinoceros horn, four qian of cyperus, a little bit of dragon brain.

Grind these into a powder, and for each dose, use half a copper coin, decocted with peach kernel soup as a medium. For infants under one year old, use half a coin.

Mr. Mao's formula: Treats all kinds of wheezing in children.

Sea cicada, black bindweed powder, oyster shell, and peeled Aristolochia.

Take each of these ingredients in equal amounts of two qian, mix them into a powder, and for each dose, use one qian, taken with a light broth made from crucian carp. [99p]
Sea Cucumber and Oyster Calcined
Grind them into equal parts, take one qian each time, and mix with a light ginger decoction to ingest.

Er Sheng San
Treats wind phlegm obstruction, loss of voice, shortness of breath, and tremors in hands and feet.
Ten pieces of fruit from haizi, half raw and half roasted; wash and roast five qian of large belly peel.
Grind them together, take two qian with a cup of water, boil down to seven parts and take warm at any time.

Wu He Tang
Treats cough due to excess heat in children.
Half a liang each of angelica wine wash, red poria, roasted licorice, big yellow, and bitter orange, washed and lightly roasted until slightly yellow, each seven and a half qian.
Grind and take two qian, with a cup of water, boil down to seven parts and take warm at any time.

Ding Chuan Yin
Treats cough due to wind phlegm obstruction, shortness of breath, regardless of hot or cold symptoms.
Five qian each of ginseng without the root, ephedra without cutting the root, prepared cyathula without the black skin, haizi without the pit, and pinellia washed to remove the slippery quality; licorice.
Grind them together, take two qian, with a cup of water and two slices of ginger, boil down to seven parts and take warm at any time.

Duo Ming San [from Dong Yi Bao Jian]
Treats the same as above.
One liang each of green limestone and saltpeter are combined in a pot and calcined until the saltpeter is gone; when the limestone takes on a golden color, it is ready to be used.
Grind into a powder, and take with mint juice mixed with honey. [100p]
For treating a child's cough, shortness of breath, a sensation of sucking in the chest, producing mucus and phlegm, and coughing out foul pus: burn light bamboo juice, boil it for twenty times, take one dose of one unit, five doses a day, and it will not interfere with food or milk intake.

For a child's cough: four taels of fresh ginger, brew the soup and bathe the child in it.

For a child with a cold cough or wheezing: use five pine nut kernels, stir-fried 百部 (bai bu), three fen of ephedra, and forty unskinned apricot kernels. Boil with a little water for three to five boils; dissolve white sugar, shape into balls the size of a quail's egg, and have the child dissolve ten of these after each meal.

For a child's cough that does not produce sound: mix powdered 紫菀 (zi wan) and apricot kernels in equal parts, combine with honey and grind them into balls the size of a quail's egg. Each dose is one ball, to be taken with five-flavor soup.

For sudden coughing in a child, especially if the cough has been persistent with phlegm for a hundred days: five qian of fritillaria bulbs and two qian of licorice, half-baked and half-raw, ground into powder; make sugar balls the size of a quail's egg, take one with rice wine.

For a child's phlegm and wheezing: one bean of巴豆 (ba dou) ground to paste, wrap in cotton and plug into the nose, male on the left and female on the right, phlegm will drain out naturally.

For a child's cough: two taels of bee honeycomb, wash and grind it. Each dose should be taken with a tiny amount of rice wine.

For a child with wind-cold, fever with phlegm, and unresponsiveness: half a tael of toasted 芥穗 (jie sui), and a stick of musk and powdered brain, each in small amounts, take half a qian with tea. This can also be used for adults.[101p]
For a child with wheezing: take seven live crucian carp, place them in a container, and allow the child to urinate on them to nourish them. Wait until they are thoroughly cooked and then consume; this is highly effective. One girl, aged ten, used this method and never had another episode.

For a child with wheezing, coughing, fever, and spontaneous sweating: use equal parts ginseng and tianhua powder, taking half a penny worth each time, mixed with honey water, using this as a standard for dosage.

For a child with wheezing and cough (nasal congestion), use a small amount of glutinous rice water, grind tea seeds, and drip them into the nose, allowing the child to inhale and swallow. Have the child bite on a bamboo tube; after a short time, saliva will emerge in threads. Doing this two or three times eliminates the problem, as often verified.

For a child with phlegm-related wheezing, cough, and persistent heat in the diaphragm: take one guo lou fruit, remove the seeds and grind it to a powder. Mix it with cold food flour to make small cakes, cook them until golden, then grind again. Take one penny's worth each time, dissolved in warm water, three times a day, stopping once effective.

For a child with wind-phlegm: take a small amount of copper vitriol powder, mix it with warmed vinegar soup, and it will induce vomiting of phlegm, swiftly bringing relief.

For a child with phlegm wheezing who does not improve with medication: take one egg from a hen, obtain the clear part, add ten pennies of light powder, mix well, place in a silver container, and steam it in a pot until cooked. A three-year-old can consume it entirely; it should induce either phlegm expulsion or diarrhea, leading to recovery. This formula is only applicable if the condition is serious.[102p]
For children who spit phlegm, it may be caused by wind obstruction or cough with fever, leading to vomiting after eating: Soak half an ounce of Pinellia in water seven times, add a small amount of clove, prepare a paste with the powder of Pinellia mixed with water and wrap the cloves, cover with dough, steam until cooked, then remove the dough and grind into powder. Mix with natural juice of ginger to make pills the size of a sesame seed, take 20-30 pills each time, swallowed with tangerine peel soup.

To treat children's cough: burn soap pod to ash and grind it finely, take half a penny or one penny each time, dissolve in fermented soybean soup at any time.

To treat various coughs and clear phlegm: use the leaves of a yellow flower, no specific amount, grind finely and place in a pot, simmer on low heat to extract the juice, let cool, then grind finely again, mix with water to form pills the size of a radish seed, take two pills with warm water before sleep.

To treat children's cough: use the skin of Trichosanthes, no specific amount, smear with honey, roast over slow fire until charred, grind into a red powder, take one penny each time and mix with honey to form a paste, apply inside the child's mouth regularly.

To alleviate children's asthma and transform phlegm: use 49 pig trotters, wash them clean and dry; in each toenail, add half an ounce of Pinellia and a pinch of alum, place in a jar and seal tightly to prevent smoke from escaping, roast with flames until red, then grind finely, add one penny of musk, and for coughing and wheezing, take with glutinous rice drink; for children, half a penny is enough.[103p]
For children with phlegm for many years, take powdered sea turtle shell, one qian mixed with rice gruel.

For children with salt-induced asthma: burn sesame stalks to retain their essence, expel fire toxins, grind to powder, and dip with plain tofu to consume.

For children with asthma: take long-standing snail powder from the south wall, mix with water, and consume at dusk while clasping hands in prayer. This proves effective.

For children with phlegm heat, cough, and fright: mix equal parts of Pinellia and South Star, grind to powder, mix with ox bile, dry in a windy place, and form into small pills the size of mung beans. Take three to five pills with ginger soup.

To treat children's coughs not due to adolescence: finely grind white silkworms and apply a small amount to the nipples, allowing the child to ingest; immediate effect observed.

As for acupuncture and moxibustion:

The "Complete Book of Pediatrics" states: for pediatric asthma, moxibustion should be performed at the heart point on the left back at Sanli, three times each. Also, avoid sour, salty, spicy, and hot foods.

The "Ancient and Modern Medical Compilation" mentions: for children with persistent cough, moxibustion at the lung shu point, positioned 1.5 cun beside the lower part of the third vertebra in the back.

The "Evidence-Based Treatment Principles" states: for children with swelling and asthma, popularly known as horse spleen wind or wind throat, measure the child's middle finger from the palm lines to the fingertip. Cut two grass stalks, position them slightly inclined from the milk aperture, with an upright stance and cross a third stalk at the tips, then puncture the acupoints and moxibustion three times. This method has often led to recovery.[104p]
Medical Cases

In the Qian family’s "Direct Principles," it is said: A five-year-old boy from the Du family had a cough with phlegm in mid-winter; this was due to wind and cold injuring the lungs. He was treated with Mahuang Pills to clear the lungs, followed by Ejiao Powder to nourish the lungs, repeated three times, but his condition worsened. The teacher said: "Clearing the lungs did not lead to improvement, and nourishing the lungs did not resolve the illness; there is nothing more to be done." Ultimately, he experienced severe wheezing and passed away.

Li Yunshi's son was eight years old, suffering from cough, a feeling of fullness in the chest, and shortness of breath. Some suggested that there was heat in the lung meridian and prescribed Bamboo Leaf Decoction and Niuhuang Paste, each twice a day; after three days, he experienced increased wheezing. The teacher said: "This is due to deficiency of lung qi combined with cold evil. Treat it with herbs that tonify the spleen and lungs to cure him." Using Bamboo Leaf and Niuhuang, which are heart medicines, to treat the lungs was a mistake.

Zhang family's grandson, aged nine, had wheezing and cough, felt congested, could not stop drinking water, and could not eat; he was given cooling medicines, but after a month, there was no improvement. The teacher said: "These cooling medicines harmed the stomach. Administer Yishi Powder to tonify the spleen, and Bai San to clear the lung, allowing for recovery."

Duanzhai's son, aged four, had a cough with fever, and coughed up blood for several days. Some recommended Ganju Decoction and Fangji Pill, but he had phlegm rising and could not stop coughing or wheezing. A dose of Bianyin Pill was given to purge him, followed by treatment with a powder to nourish the lungs. Some argued: "The symptoms indicate lung deficiency; why purge?" The teacher responded: "The lung meridian has heat, plus phlegm rising causes coughing spasms, so it is appropriate to first clear the phlegm and then nourish the spleen and lungs for recovery."[105p]
In "Young Science Expressed," it is stated: A child coughs, takes Baolong Pills, but instead vomits, has diarrhea, and does not breastfeed; with abdominal bloating and fever, use Liu Junzi Decoction, and both mother and child recover. Later, the mother drinks alcohol and still coughs; use Qingwei Powder with added Quya, and the mother takes it, resulting in the child's recovery as well.

A child suffers from a cough, and upon taking medications like Qingtan, vomits breast milk and develops a fever, accompanied by abdominal bloating; this indicates injury to the spleen and stomach leading to internal heat. Use Yigong Powder with added Diaoteng for gradual recovery, then take the previous medicine with added Donggui for comfort.

A child with a cough takes Niuhuang Qingxin Pills but develops panting and abdominal bloating; this indicates deficiency of spleen and lung Qi. Use Liu Junzi Decoction for immediate recovery.

Cai Shajiang, a scholar from Qishui, had a son who was ill with a cough that persisted for a long time, so he sought my treatment. When I arrived, I saw the child continuously coughing, turning pale during the cough, and shaking his right hand. I told Shajiang: Your son cannot be treated. Shajiang asked why. I replied: The cough indicates lung disease; the lung belongs to metal; the pale face reflects the liver's color; the liver belongs to wood; the shaking hand indicates the force of liver wind wanting to manifest. Wood overcomes metal, which is fearful in this condition.

October corresponds to metal, and metal is weak when wood grows; the four seasons must progress, where future elements advance, and successful elements retreat. Fire promotes growth, metal suffers and recedes; convulsions are untreatable. The critical days of Jia and Yi came. Indeed, on those days, he convulsed and died.[106p]
The "Medical Overview" states: Wind in the lungs often begins with a cough, but if one only takes cough medicine, it cannot dispel the wind pathogen that has entered the lung channels. This leads to urgent wheezing, a complexion of green and yellow, the ability to recognize others but an inability to speak. If the physician cannot make a clear diagnosis and waits passively, is this not a disgrace? The daughter of the Minister Wang from Shaoxing accompanied an old woman who suffered from this illness and died after half a month; common physicians were unable to recognize it. Zhang Nanxuan also contracted this illness and passed away. Later, the son of Lou Bage fell ill with similar symptoms. At that time, it was a singular qi issue, and all physicians said there was no remedy and withdrew. The father and son came to urgently seek help, and I went to examine him. I prepared a decoction of three ingredients: tangerine peel, white mulberry bark, and poppy husk, combined it with two doses of Baibu pills, and applied moxa on the lung shu point. His wheezing immediately ceased, and he could suddenly speak, then asked for porridge, thus he was saved.

The "Golden Mirror of Infant Care" states: A child suffered from a cough and took the Niu Huang Qingxin Pill, but presented with severe wheezing and abdominal distension. Upon examination, I found that his right cheek was red and the pulse was patterned like a spear, indicating damage to the spleen qi; I used Liu Junzi Decoction to bring immediate relief.[107p]
